<div id="review_105170021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105170021" />
    <a title="Paula Gallagher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2549508-paula-gallagher"><img alt="Paula Gallagher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582510169p2/2549508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105170021?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula Gallagher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula Gallagher" href="/user/show/2549508-paula-gallagher">Paula Gallagher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105170021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13833886467368312265">It's a shame this YA paranormal doesn't live up to its winning premise and eyecatchingly creepy cover. <br/><br/>The writing reminds me of the unpolished work of a high school girl--all breathless, dreary atmosphere;utterly lacking in language. Descriptions of people and place are spare and trite. The characters are disappointingly cliche and the world under the slag heap needs a whole lot more fleshing out, so to speak. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_90037699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90037699" />
    <a title="Misty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1124284-misty"><img alt="Misty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539720622p2/1124284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90037699?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misty" href="/user/show/1124284-misty">Misty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=cover-appeal">cover-appeal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=ala-2010">ala-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=juvenile-ya">juvenile-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=arc-or-galley">arc-or-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=excited-for">excited-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=folklore-myth-fable-fairy-tall-tale">folklore-myth-fable-fairy-tall-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=horror-mystery-suspense-thriller">horror-mystery-suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=supernatural-paranormal">supernatural-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=helluva-halloween">helluva-halloween</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90037699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5883772854771154593">Months ago, someone on Goodreads posted this as to read and I went a little wild over this cover. I mean, come on.  I was determined I was going to get my hands on it, but it's not all that often that I'll actively pursue a review copy of something.  I figured I'd just have to wait until it's release to read it.  So imagine my excitement when I got a copy of it at ALA.  (*ooh, little frisson of excitement still*)   So that was a little too easy.  And we all know what generally happens to me when</span>
  <span id="freeText5883772854771154593" style="display:none">Months ago, someone on Goodreads posted this as to read and I went a little wild over this cover. I mean, come on.  I was determined I was going to get my hands on it, but it's not all that often that I'll actively pursue a review copy of something.  I figured I'd just have to wait until it's release to read it.  So imagine my excitement when I got a copy of it at ALA.  (*ooh, little frisson of excitement still*)   So that was a little too easy.  And we all know what generally happens to me when I go gaga over a cover (*cough*<a href="http://bookrat-misty.blogspot.com/2010/02/hush-hush-part-i-spoiler-filled.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Hush, Hush</a>*cough*).  Also, even though I like them lots, faerie stories tend to disappoint, too.  So this was bound to let me down, right?<br /><br />Didn't matter, I still wanted to read it.  But I decided I was going to save it for Helluva Halloween, and that made me happy and gave me something to look forward to.  I can't even count all the times I started to pick it up early, but I was trying to be good. (And I was successful.  Point for me!)<br /><br />Now it's Helluva Halloween, and I finally go to read it.  And what can I say?  Maybe, just <i>maybe</i>, the cover/faerie curse is broken.  This has been one of my favorite reads this year, and I have no hesitation in saying that.  When I went on vacation earlier in the month, when everyone else was gathered around a bonfire drinking and getting rowdy, I went upstairs to read this.  Yeah.  I've been hesitant to write this review because, as I've said before, it's sometimes just as hard to write about something you loved as it is something you hated.  I don't even know where to start.<br /><br />Mackie is a replacement, what would often be called a changeling, and he spends his life struggling to fit in and keep this very dangerous secret.  But as hard as he's always tried to pretend -- and to <i>be --</i> normal, Mackie can't hide who he is forever.  The iron that fills the modern world is toxic to him, and he's slowly dying of it.  This struggle was sort of enthralling to read.  I felt bad for Mackie, partly because he's so very much an outsider (of the community's doing, yes, but more so of his own.  Not w/o reason, but still...), and partly because he just doesn't realize how miserably he's failing.  He's hurting, and he's scared and lonely, and he's so grateful for the people that love him -- it's like reading about yourself at your most raw and insecure.  I don't think it's possible to not relate to Mackie or feel for him.<br /><br />But I don't want to give them impression that this is some pathetic sob-story, because it's not.  There's just this level of thought and insight, this depth that I wasn't expecting, but that heightened the whole experience for me.  Mackie's story, and the town of Gentry, is really dark and unflinching.  I've read a lot of reviews that call the book scary, and I don't think that it's ever really <i>that</i>.  It's more that it can be so unsettlingly real and human in the best <i>and </i>worst ways that it gets under your skin.  And that can be scary.<br /><br />I don't want to go too into detail because I don't want to start giving things away, but I do want to talk a little bit about the Yavonoff's writing and the choices she made.  On the former, the writing is lovely.  It flows beautifully, and I always had a clear image of the characters, the town and the emotions behind it all.  Which leads me to the latter -- Yavonoff did some really wonderful things with a straightforward story.  It's a typical outsider tale, very appropriate for YA with its discovery and near-coming of age quality.  But it's enriched with so much emotion and understanding that it's sort of transformative.  Yavonoff does something really lovely with human connections in this book, with both romantic love and familial love, and (to be really repetitive) I loved that.  Her depiction of love isn't sugary and sappy and over the top as it is in many YAs, and it's balanced with the dark and creepy that exists side-by-side in the book.  All together it gives this great dimension*, these highs and lows that make it dynamic and unputdownable and delicious.<br /><br />So read it.  Preferably now, as the days are getting short and dark.<br /><br />Bonus Shenanigans:<br /><br /><a href="http://bookrat-misty.blogspot.com/2010/10/guest-post-from-author-brenna-yavonoff.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Brenna Yavonoff guest post</a> <br /><a href="http://bookrat-misty.blogspot.com/2010/10/character-connection-cutter.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Character Connection: the Cutter</a><br /><a href="http://bookrat-misty.blogspot.com/2010/10/teaser-replacement-by-brenna-yavonoff.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Teaser of The Replacement</a><br /><br /><br />*originally read "demention"  &lt;-- ha!  The Cutter may be demented, as is the Lady, assuredly, but the book is not.<br /><br />[Please note: I read an ARC of this book, so the final version may differ.] </span>
  <a data-text-id="5883772854771154593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2151975277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2151975277" />
    <a title="Janie Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson"><img alt="Janie Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486148700p2/5116650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2151975277?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janie Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janie Johnson" href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson">Janie Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5116650-janie-johnson?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2151975277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2476645470865778737">At first I thought this was going to be a middle grade horror, but discovered it is more YA just because there is a small amount of language that is definitely not suitable for younger kiddos!<br/><br/>I picked this book up last month at our local UBS actually because of my niece Rylee. She likes to read middle grade and YA Horror so it made me start looking for it. I figured if she is a book lover and she likes middle grade or YA horror, then I was certain to as well. So I found this one and was pretty i</span>
  <span id="freeText2476645470865778737" style="display:none">At first I thought this was going to be a middle grade horror, but discovered it is more YA just because there is a small amount of language that is definitely not suitable for younger kiddos!<br /><br />I picked this book up last month at our local UBS actually because of my niece Rylee. She likes to read middle grade and YA Horror so it made me start looking for it. I figured if she is a book lover and she likes middle grade or YA horror, then I was certain to as well. So I found this one and was pretty intrigued by both the cover and the synopsis. I had never read a book quite like this one before and it had me right from the start. <br /><br />There are some pretty disturbing aspects to this story and for Horror, that is very important to me. I was a bit confused at the beginning as to who knew what was going on with Mackie, but it resolved itself the further I went into the story. It is not that the book was 'scary' but it was pretty creepy. I loved the setting I think the most in this book. Creepy small town with a good side and a bad side, but the creepiest part was that the good side was bad and the bad side was abominable. I LOVED THAT! I love the whole feeling of a town that had some ghosts in the closet. but everything was fine.<br /><br />I also loved the characters in this book. So different but with such a sinister, ghoulish side that they could not see themselves. There are plenty of good characters, bad characters, and those detestable characters that we all love to hate. There was definitely a good mix of personalities in this one. I think IK would have to say that Mackie was my most favorite character, I love what he stood for and what he was willing to give up for the people he loved the most. Then Tate came in at a close second, she is a character who knows what's up and wont take crap from people.<br /><br />Overall I enjoyed the story a lot and I wish there was a book 2 but pretty sure there is not going to be. This is definitely worth the read. So I will look for more of this author and definitely will look for more YA or MG horror! </span>
  <a data-text-id="2476645470865778737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_892129652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/892129652" />
    <a title="Amanda " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28146201-amanda"><img alt="Amanda " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541846541p2/28146201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/892129652?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda " href="/user/show/28146201-amanda">Amanda </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer892129652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13295534168741957232">This book contained everything I could ask for in a story and more. <u>The Replacement</u> is an eerie book that kept me up late at night. It falls into my favorite genre, paranormal/fantasy romance, and it actually does the genre justice. My only complaint is that I wanted a little more in the romance aspect. I wasn't really sold on Mackie and Tate's romance. It's been a LONG time since I've read a book from a male point of view, and I found myself enjoying that aspect of this book a lot more than I t</span>
  <span id="freeText13295534168741957232" style="display:none">This book contained everything I could ask for in a story and more. <u>The Replacement</u> is an eerie book that kept me up late at night. It falls into my favorite genre, paranormal/fantasy romance, and it actually does the genre justice. My only complaint is that I wanted a little more in the romance aspect. I wasn't really sold on Mackie and Tate's romance. It's been a LONG time since I've read a book from a male point of view, and I found myself enjoying that aspect of this book a lot more than I thought I would. <br /><br />I really loved the characters. Tate is my favorite because she reminds me of myself when I was a teenager. I loved Emma too, she is such a great sister and there is real unconditional love for her brother shown in this story. Mackie was pretty great too, he's a misfit and I really felt that he grew throughout the story. Roswell was such a good, loyal friend, which is something that I always admire in real life. <br /><br />I really liked the whole idea of this story. I felt that it was incredibly original, which has been pretty hard to find lately. The world building was pretty good. At times I felt that I was a little confused, and I felt that the first half of the book moved a little slow for me. This is the only reason that I'm giving the book four stars instead of five. When I read the plot summary I immediately put this one on my TBR. <b>
  <i>I was so grateful to be able to receive this book as part of the traveling book program in the All About Fantasy group on Goodreads.</i>
</b> <br /><br />I don't think there is a sequel, but I wish that there was. I really loved the characters and would like to see the Morrigan and The House of Mayhem again. This was a great introduction to Brenna Yovanoff's work and I will certainly be on the lookout for anything else that she writes. She created a world that I found so fascinating, I can't wait to see what she comes up with next.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13295534168741957232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1588184673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1588184673" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8104446-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453203748p2/8104446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1588184673?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/8104446-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1588184673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12806617211011791622"><b>The Replacement</b> by Brenna Yovanoff<br/>4★'s<br/><br/>From The Cover:<br/>Mackie Doyle is not one of us. Though he lives in the small town of Gentry, he comes from a world of tunnels and black murky water, a world of living dead girls ruled by a little tattooed princess. He is a Replacement, left in the crib of a human baby sixteen years ago. Now, because of fatal allergies to iron, blood, and consecrated ground, Mackie is fighting to survive in the human world. Mackie would give anything to live among us, to practi</span>
  <span id="freeText12806617211011791622" style="display:none"><b>The Replacement</b> by Brenna Yovanoff<br />4★'s<br /><br />From The Cover:<br />Mackie Doyle is not one of us. Though he lives in the small town of Gentry, he comes from a world of tunnels and black murky water, a world of living dead girls ruled by a little tattooed princess. He is a Replacement, left in the crib of a human baby sixteen years ago. Now, because of fatal allergies to iron, blood, and consecrated ground, Mackie is fighting to survive in the human world. Mackie would give anything to live among us, to practice on his bass or spend time with his crush, Tate. But when Tate's baby sister goes missing, Mackie is drawn irrevocably into the underworld of Gentry, known as Mayhem. He must face the dark creatures of the Slag Heaps and find his rightful place, in our world, or theirs. <br /><br />My Thoughts:<br />An excellent read and recommended by a friend. The book is classed as "Young Adult" but that didn't erase anything from the well told story line. I have read other books buy this author and she has an easy, smooth writing style that really keeps the reader staying around, anxious to see what happens next. Other than a cast of mostly young, (teens)...characters the reader soon forgets that it was written and designed for a younger audience. One of the outstanding things that I found in this story was that Mackie understood why his parents behaved the way they did and he respected and loved them in spite of he not agreeing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12806617211011791622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p/41vVc7r+iqxjPHDg4zdwINxtqAgdO2eRKRtGuQMCbhDWbd/MMb9NMKJ7qvv9ZoUH48G6GB2YmWiCwqd4xAcA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oOY+Gviw2YRPqU4ctPktObUgU7kfFZJj6J/9tmzdcJHmFW16U0htmDZlWmEVSMgm51OpeD4VmFwHBUAocMEAxw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
